**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines.

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

Scoring: 

Some articles are better than others, with more prestigious and reliable sources, and more factual, relevant, concise titles. So, you need to give every news article an importance score, from 1 to 10, 1 as the least important, 10 as the most important. Remember to use a consistent standard across all articles. Then, considering the importance of the topic itself, and the weight of all news reports on that topic, and then give an importance score for the topic, from 1 to 10, 1 as the least important, 10 as the most important. Remember not to saturate the scale! Use "importance 10" sparingly. And then, in the same way, give an importance score for the area containing multiple topics. 

Do this consistently for all news articles, topics and areas. Please insert the importance scores into their JSON lines, by creating a value called "importance" and insert it after "title", but keep everything else untouched. Compile all your results in a simple text file (step3.txt).

The Pentagon's specialized technology unit, described as a "SWAT team of nerds," has resigned en masse [237, 348], with the program's director reportedly stating, "either we die quickly or we die slowly." This upheaval coincides with a leak probe affecting Pentagon leadership, with top Hegseth adviser Dan Caldwell being placed on leave [273, 313]. Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth is dismantling Pentagon programs designed to reduce civilian casualties, with his focus on "lethality" prompting warnings from one Pentagon official that this approach could lead to "wanton killing and wholesale destruction and disregard for law" [300]. In a separate development, sources indicate President Trump plans to name a Hunter Biden whistleblower as acting IRS commissioner [350], suggesting continued restructuring across multiple federal agencies.

## Area 2: Immigration and Deportation Policies (Importance: 7)

### Topic 2.1: Deportation Actions and Enforcement (Importance: 7)
The Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE) is reportedly accessing data from federal agencies to identify and remove immigrants from housing [236], representing an expansion of deportation infrastructure. Immigration enforcement actions have sparked legal challenges, with a Colorado judge implementing a temporary hold on deportations sought under the Alien Enemies Act [246]. Controversial cases have emerged, including ICE's deportation of a Venezuelan teenager despite reportedly knowing he was not a target [302], with reports indicating agents were told to "take him anyway" [331]. The Trump administration appears to be accelerating deportation efforts, with moves to expedite asylum cases without court hearings [306] and statements from President Trump expressing interest in deporting American citizens to El Salvador, with Trump quoted as saying "I Would Love to Do That" [287]. A White House Press Secretary has reportedly acknowledged plans to deport citizens [316]. These actions have prompted judicial responses, with one federal judge blocking an attempt to strip deportation protections from approximately 500,000 immigrants, describing it as "unlawful action" [281]. The administration has also terminated an immigration lawyer who argued the case of a mistakenly deported individual [266], highlighting tensions between deportation policies and legal representation.

## 2. Immigration and Deportation Policies

### 2.1 Deportation Actions and Legal Battles
A Colorado judge has implemented a temporary hold on deportations sought under the Alien Enemies Act [1]. Controversial cases include ICE's deportation of a Venezuelan teenager despite reportedly knowing he was not a target [2], with reports indicating agents were told to "take him anyway" [3]. The Trump administration is accelerating deportation efforts, with moves to expedite asylum cases without court hearings [4] and statements from President Trump expressing interest in deporting American citizens to El Salvador, with Trump quoted as saying "I Would Love to Do That" [5]. A federal judge blocked an attempt to strip deportation protections from approximately 500,000 immigrants, describing it as "unlawful action" [6].

### 2.2 The Abrego Garcia Case
The case of Kilmar Abrego Garcia, deported to El Salvador, has become a focal point for legal challenges. A federal judge ordered expedited discovery [1] and will question Trump officials regarding their refusal to return Abrego Garcia to the United States [2]. The judge noted that the "Supreme Court has spoken" and criticized the administration for doing "nothing" to facilitate his return [3]. The court is considering contempt proceedings against the Trump administration [4]. Maryland Senator Van Hollen has indicated he might travel to El Salvador to seek Abrego Garcia's return [5], with other Democratic lawmakers planning to join this delegation [6].

## 3. Federal Funding and Institutional Relations

### 3.1 Higher Education Funding Disputes
A significant funding dispute has erupted between President Trump and Harvard University, with the administration freezing more than $2.2 billion after Harvard rejected certain presidential demands [1]. Trump has threatened to revoke Harvard's tax-exempt status [2]. Former President Obama has characterized Trump's freeze of Harvard funding as "unlawful" [3] and "ham-handed and illegal" [4]. While Harvard has taken a firm stance, Columbia University remains in negotiations regarding its federal funding [5]. Harvard Law faculty have characterized the administration's approach as a "page straight out of authoritarian playbooks" [6]. The funding dispute appears to be affecting student choices, with Canadian universities reporting increases in applications from US students [7].

## 5. Trade, Tariffs and Economic Policies

### 5.1 US-China Trade Relations and Tariff Impacts
US-China trade relations have deteriorated into a trade war, with analysts warning that "this is going to get really ugly" [1]. China has ordered a halt to Boeing jet deliveries as the trade war expands [2], causing Boeing shares to fall [3]. The president's threat to impose tariffs on drug imports reportedly poses "big political risks" [4], while the administration has launched a probe into critical minerals that could lead to new tariffs [5]. The White House's negotiating approach using "shock and awe tariffs" faces challenges in finding a "first mover" for fast negotiations [6]. Public perception of economic conditions appears negative, with a majority of Americans reportedly believing the economy is "getting worse" under Trump [7].

The Trump administration is evaluating significant changes to America's diplomatic footprint, with reports indicating plans to close nearly 30 overseas embassies and consulates [1]. US-Canada relations have taken an unusual turn, with a White House representative reiterating that "Trump believes Canada would 'benefit greatly' from becoming 51st state" [2]. Vice President JD Vance has expressed optimism about UK-US trade relations, indicating a "good chance" of a trade deal and noting that "Trump 'really loves' Britain" [3]. In contrast, European Union relations appear strained, with reports that "EU Staff Is Now Using Burner Phones to Evade Trump" [4]. Canadian academic institutions are responding cautiously to US immigration policies, with university teachers being warned against traveling to the United States [5].
